<div id="review_2151431513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2151431513" />
    <a title="Michael Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72416163-michael-campbell"><img alt="Michael Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583366142p2/72416163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2151431513?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Campbell" href="/user/show/72416163-michael-campbell">Michael Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2151431513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16727020220000527645">I spent the entire time I've read this series wondering about how it'll end. Every little time jump gave me new ideas for possibilities, and I continually updated my most likely conclusion. I had something of an anxiety about it, as I often do with grand epic works of fiction. How could one possibly end it both decisively and satisfactorily? Well, Isaac Asimov figured it out, and I can't help but wonder whether or not this was the plan all along or if he realized the conclusion along with Treviz</span>
  <span id="freeText16727020220000527645" style="display:none">I spent the entire time I've read this series wondering about how it'll end. Every little time jump gave me new ideas for possibilities, and I continually updated my most likely conclusion. I had something of an anxiety about it, as I often do with grand epic works of fiction. How could one possibly end it both decisively and satisfactorily? Well, Isaac Asimov figured it out, and I can't help but wonder whether or not this was the plan all along or if he realized the conclusion along with Trevize. <br /><br />It was nice we were able to keep the same basic cast from the last book, as we got to find out Isaac Asimov isn't half so bad at writing characters with solid development. The different worlds and cultures they encounter were all brilliantly depicted, realized, and just neat to be honest. <br /><br />Most of this review is going to be entirely spoilers, because I can't seem to come up with a way of talking about this book in detail without giving spoilers. <br /><br /> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Okay so I've seen the pros and cons of a hive mind type society argued a time or two. Never really in a piece of fiction at this level of excellence, and the ending of the novel made me sit up last night wondering about it. It seems such an obvious conclusion to the end of the novel, but the whole time I felt the same displeasure with the idea that Trevize did.<br /><br />However, I became convinced at the end that in this set scenario, it's really the only way to go. As separate entities, we'll always have conflict no matter the societal restrictions we place on ourselves. This was admirably displayed throughout the series and particularly in this novel with the different isolated worlds visited. <br /><br />Galaxia is a bit easier to swallow after following along with Bliss and seeing she still does retain independent thought and personality. She is apart of Gaia and has the collected memories and feelings of Gaia to draw from, but it is shown that she has her own feelings, makes her own decisions(albeit often influenced by Gaia), and has a distinct personality. <br /><br />The Seldon Plan not factoring in outside influences became obvious with The Mule. An unexpected mutated human being nearly overthrew the system, so just imagine, what an incursion from an alien species capable of traveling between galaxies could do to it. <br /><br />In the end, this book made me a proponent of something I never thought I'd support. The concept of the hive mind detailed in this book really does seem like a realistic conclusion for humanity. How can we defend ourselves from others when we can't stop bickering for ten minutes? Just imagine where we would be at technologically speaking if we lived in a constant renaissance, without the wasted effort we've spent on wars throughout our history. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="16727020220000527645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1701610315" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1701610315" />
    <a title="Ivana Books Are Magic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56173179-ivana-books-are-magic"><img alt="Ivana Books Are Magic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578249636p2/56173179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1701610315?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivana Books Are Magic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivana Books Are Magic" href="/user/show/56173179-ivana-books-are-magic">Ivana Books Are Magic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780553900941" href="/book/show/9908090-foundation-and-earth">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1701610315" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5917352708955063562"><br/>Just thinking about Foundation and Earth brings a smile to my face. Does that ever happen to you? I almost wish I could repeat that experience of reading it for the first time. This book is very much my cup of tea. The only reason why I'm giving this novel four and not five stars is that reading it wasn't a life-changing experience. It was a very pleasant one and perhaps that's it. Not that it was predictable for it certainly wasn't. On the contrary, there were some nice twists and turns that ma</span>
  <span id="freeText5917352708955063562" style="display:none"><br />Just thinking about Foundation and Earth brings a smile to my face. Does that ever happen to you? I almost wish I could repeat that experience of reading it for the first time. This book is very much my cup of tea. The only reason why I'm giving this novel four and not five stars is that reading it wasn't a life-changing experience. It was a very pleasant one and perhaps that's it. Not that it was predictable for it certainly wasn't. On the contrary, there were some nice twists and turns that made me wonder and shake my head, but trust to Asimov to tie it all perfectly together. These novel showcases Asimov’s strengths as a writer: great story, plausible plot and fantastic imaginative scope. It may be that what makes it so enjoyable to read, is what takes away that x factor.<br /><br /> It was easy to get lost in the story and I did like the characters a great deal. Reading it was a breeze. Perhaps that is it, maybe it just felt too easy. As a fan, I came with certain expectations and when these were met, I didn't ask for me. Perhaps I should have meditated upon this one a bit more but it felt so complete there seemed no need. <br /><br />The dialogues were, not surprisingly, my favourite part of the novel. Some say that Asimov doesn't develops his characters well enough, but I beg to differ. He doesn't broad over them but he reveals a lot about them in dialogues they have with one another. Furthermore, his characters are often defined by their actions. Asimov may believe that deeds matter more than words. Actions are often better indicators of a person's personality than words. Sometimes these dialogues tend to get very philosophical even to the point of slowing the narrative, but I happen to like them. It is great being able to see contrasting points of view and one can certainly see them in this novel.<br /><br /> The plot itself was very well developed. I quite liked the narrative. This search for Earth seemed so romantic and beautiful in its essence. This concept humankind (i.e., representatives of humankind) looking for their long lost home (whatever they reason may be). I found it very touching. The exploration of different worlds and hence cultures was masterfully done. The characters didn't undergo much personal development, but they felt real. I think dialogues and actions they take spoke loads about them, so no need for long descriptions and passages on their mind.<br /><br />I felt a sense of connection with the characters but also with the story. The narrative moved me on an emotional level, but not too deeply. I sympathized with the characters but I didn't agonize over them. I took up this book expecting that I would love it. I can't say that I was disappointed because this novel was everything I wished it to be. Intelligent, well written story with memorable characters. That's what I expected and that's what I got. So, no complains. I didn't have a feeling that my soul was stirred or that my life was changed by this book but I did felt engaged in it. My mind was active while I was reading it and my heart was responding to it as well.<br /><br /> Is there something I didn't like about this novel? Honesty, no. I really can't think of something that needs improving. There is nothing I would change about the way it is written. I see a lot of readers here complaining about the ending. I didn't have a problem with the ending. I quite liked it actually. I didn't see it coming and that was a nice surprise. It makes it even better. On overall, I think the ending ties everything nicely. If you ask me, this is a great sf novel. In other words, Asimov doing his thing. Thank you Isaac for another wonderful novel!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5917352708955063562" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_168814607" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168814607" />
    <a title="Toby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5454475-toby"><img alt="Toby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542247337p2/5454475.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168814607?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Toby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Toby" href="/user/show/5454475-toby">Toby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780586071106" href="/book/show/837143.Foundation_and_Earth">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168814607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3155055767216036516">The End.<br/><br/>This 15 book sequence is missing only those two words. This is later Asimov and you can tell, he really learned how to tell a story by this point. I loved this book, it was easily my favourite of the Foundation books and right up there with the best Lije Baley/R.Daneel Olivaw books.<br/><br/>The excitement of the adventure in this one really captivated me, the journey for Earth something that has been hinted at repeatedly from the early Empire trilogy right through to Trevize and Pelorat finally t</span>
  <span id="freeText3155055767216036516" style="display:none">The End.<br /><br />This 15 book sequence is missing only those two words. This is later Asimov and you can tell, he really learned how to tell a story by this point. I loved this book, it was easily my favourite of the Foundation books and right up there with the best Lije Baley/R.Daneel Olivaw books.<br /><br />The excitement of the adventure in this one really captivated me, the journey for Earth something that has been hinted at repeatedly from the early Empire trilogy right through to Trevize and Pelorat finally taking the journey in this final book. And boy was it worth it, I don't think I've ever read 510 pages in so short a space of time, I was enjoying myself so much.<br /><br />I have problems with some of the wishy washy concepts banded about in this one BUT I can't argue with the way Asimov explains them or tells their story; the constant bickering of Bliss and Trevize could esily have become irritating for example but the way they're presented here is nothing but entertaining.<br /><br />I find myself conflicted having now finished the sequence, I am relieved it's over allowing me to finally fully contemplate the vast scope of the journey from Susan Calvin to Galaxia and appreciate exactly what was achieved by Asimov in linking all the different stories together but I also find myself sad that there is no more to come, not Foundation and Galaxia for example or Galaxia and Andromeda even. I can however console myself with the fact that of all my favourite authors Dr Asimov was one of the most prolific in terms of fiction (second only to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9693.Georges_Simenon" title="Georges Simenon" rel="nofollow noopener">Georges Simenon</a>) and there's still plenty more to read.<br /><br />I highly recommend reading these books in the suggested reading order provided by Asimov, the overall effect is extremely rewarding.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3155055767216036516" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2404415498" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2404415498" />
    <a title="Cheryl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3498889-cheryl"><img alt="Cheryl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590863781p2/3498889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2404415498?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/3498889-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2404415498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9630439211366355623">Ok, I guess that I'm glad I read it. But actually I wish Asimov hadn't written it. It's poorly written, and it makes no sense. A novelette worth of episodes scattered amongst the characters educating each other about the history of mankind and about astronomy, because they each have their own specialties. <br/><br/>And the societal norms 20K yrs on are almost identical to ours. For example, the woman is presumed by several different populations to 'belong' to one or the other man. And when our heroes meet</span>
  <span id="freeText9630439211366355623" style="display:none">Ok, I guess that I'm glad I read it. But actually I wish Asimov hadn't written it. It's poorly written, and it makes no sense. A novelette worth of episodes scattered amongst the characters educating each other about the history of mankind and about astronomy, because they each have their own specialties. <br /><br />And the societal norms 20K yrs on are almost identical to ours. For example, the woman is presumed by several different populations to 'belong' to one or the other man. And when our heroes meet a young hermaphrodite, they decide that they must choose a gender for it, and choose female, so they can refer to the child as 'she.' Never mind that the child is actually prepubescent and therefore only would have gender in potential anyway, just as children who are not hermaphroditic would, anyway. I would not have been surprised if there had been tamping of tobacco in pipes and neat whiskey.<br /><br />Also, not sure what Rachel means about 'last novel'... what about Foundation #6... didn't Asimov write that? Well, I don't care. This (and the first) is all I could stomach of the Foundation series. <br /><br />"I understand where you are. I, too, preferred the Robot books over the Foundation. But if you want to see what eventually happens to the Spacer worlds, there is one book you'll have to read: Foundation and Earth (Foundation #5).... This book is unlike any other Foundation book and is the last novel that Asimov wrote.... In it, the Robot, Empire, and Foundation series all meet and reveal themselves to be in the same universe. You will see what happened to the Spacers; it's really awesome. I couldn't read it fast enough."<br /><br />Rachel Adiyah, Evolution of SF Group</span>
  <a data-text-id="9630439211366355623" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1446387249" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1446387249" />
    <a title="Davyne DeSye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49054501-davyne-desye"><img alt="Davyne DeSye" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538613956p2/49054501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1446387249?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Davyne DeSye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Davyne DeSye" href="/user/show/49054501-davyne-desye">Davyne DeSye</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1446387249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6041829546669853159">Loved this one (again), although it is always sad to read the last book in a series you love… because then what? I’ve been immersed in this universe for three months now, and I’m… Done. Sad. Yet fulfilling. Can’t wait to read it all again.<br/><br/>This book is so much more than the last book of Asimov’s Foundation series. It works well as the last book because, despite the fact that the two Foundations of the series are not much featured in this book, there is an ending that helps the reader look forward</span>
  <span id="freeText6041829546669853159" style="display:none">Loved this one (again), although it is always sad to read the last book in a series you love… because then what? I’ve been immersed in this universe for three months now, and I’m… Done. Sad. Yet fulfilling. Can’t wait to read it all again.<br /><br />This book is so much more than the last book of Asimov’s Foundation series. It works well as the last book because, despite the fact that the two Foundations of the series are not much featured in this book, there is an ending that helps the reader look forward to… whatever comes next (with a pretty scary hint of what comes next in the final chapter of the book!).<br /><br />I say this book is so much more because it also takes you on two additional journeys. First, this book is essentially about one man’s (okay, okay: two men and a woman’s) quest to find the legendary and long lost Earth – reputed original home of humanity. This by itself is something that fills me with melancholy. I mean, I’ve dealt with the idea in the previous books that Earth is merely “legend” and that no one is really sure that there is such a planet or that it was humanity’s original home, etc. But, in this book, you are really forced to focus on the fact that Home (yes, with a capital-H) has been abandoned and forgotten. The melancholy – or even sadness – feels akin to what it would be like discovering that your childhood home that you have so many great memories about has been abandoned, left to rot, even covered in graffiti… I can’t help the “How? How could this happen? How could we have let this happen?” feeling.<br /><br />Second, this book is the capstone for Asimov’s three series – the Robot series, the Galactic Empire series and the Foundation series. As our two heroes, Trevise and Janov, and our heroine, Bliss, traverse the universe looking for clues of the whereabouts (or existence) of Earth, they search through legends, myths, histories… anything they can find for clues. In all of that, there are references to stories in various books throughout the three series (which do in fact cover, all-in-all, 20,000 years of history in this universe). It’s the reason I read all three series in a row. I love that nostalgic feeling of “Oh, yeah, I remember that story, I miss that character.” Of course, each of the books in the entire three series could be read as a standalone book, but, how much richer the experience of the entire tapestry. I want to clarify for the person who might be considering reading only this book (or only this series), the references to books in the previous series do not leave the reader confused or lacking information – they are presented in this book as legend and myth and work very well as such.<br /><br />Sigh. Probably another five years before I read these series again, but it has been a wonderful ride. I highly recommend this book and this series to anyone who loves classic, universe-spanning science fiction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6041829546669853159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('M0WeUumzSACtT68qQfl0sYQKi20K/ZGsT+HG1IVoPLDvOhinDugF7VRLDx/nhl/pu45kUNjUzoOnU25M/xlsQw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uX5NNmAJuBXL+T/jyua3BFZs12EaetPBNZLI7mlo/oBlAcvDh1L1+DL9n9ZsmZxcaeg4XMhTjO7dIGB2Exmucw==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov">About Isaac Asimov</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1341965730p3/16667.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov">Isaac Asimov
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9617968044536284238">Isaac Asimov was a Russian-born, American author, a professor of biochemistry, and a highly successful writer, best known for his works of science fiction and for his popular science books.<br/><br/>Professor Asimov is generally considered one of the most prolific writers of all time, having written or edited more than 500 books and an estimated 90,000 letters and postcards. He has works published in nine o</span>
  <span id="freeText9617968044536284238" style="display:none">Isaac Asimov was a Russian-born, American author, a professor of biochemistry, and a highly successful writer, best known for his works of science fiction and for his popular science books.<br /><br />Professor Asimov is generally considered one of the most prolific writers of all time, having written or edited more than 500 books and an estimated 90,000 letters and postcards. He has works published in nine of the ten major categories of the Dewey Decimal System (lacking only an entry in the 100s category of Philosophy).<br /><br />Asimov is widely considered a master of the science-fiction genre and, along with Robert A. Heinlein and Arthur C. Clarke, was considered one of the "Big Three" science-fiction writers during his lifetime. Asimov's most famous work is the Foundation Series; his other major series are the Galactic Empire series and the Robot series, both of which he later tied into the same fictional universe as the Foundation Series to create a unified "future history" for his stories much like those pioneered by Robert A. Heinlein and previously produced by Cordwainer Smith and Poul Anderson. He penned numerous short stories, among them "Nightfall", which in 1964 was voted by the Science Fiction Writers of America the best short science fiction story of all time, a title many still honor. He also wrote mysteries and fantasy, as well as a great amount of nonfiction. Asimov wrote the Lucky Starr series of juvenile science-fiction novels using the pen name Paul French.<br /><br />Most of Asimov's popularized science books explain scientific concepts in a historical way, going as far back as possible to a time when the science in question was at its simplest stage. He often provides nationalities, birth dates, and death dates for the scientists he mentions, as well as etymologies and pronunciation guides for technical terms. Examples include his Guide to Science, the three volume set Understanding Physics, and Asimov's Chronology of Science and Discovery.<br /><br />Asimov was a long-time member and Vice President of Mensa International, albeit reluctantly; he described some members of that organization as "brain-proud and aggressive about their IQs" He took more joy in being president of the American Humanist Association. The asteroid 5020 Asimov, the magazine Asimov's Science Fiction, a Brooklyn, NY elementary school, and two different Isaac Asimov Awards are named in his honor.<br /><br />----------------------------------------<br /><i>Isaac Asimov. (2007, November 29). In Wikipedia, The Free Encyclopedia. Retrieved 21:50, November 29, 2007, from <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Asimov">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_As...</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9617968044536284238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_76679').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_76679').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_76679').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>
